# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the
code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What It Is

**Status:** `consistent` (README) / `drifted` (CLAUDE.md portfolio-context)
**Evidence:** `src-tauri/src/commands/mod.rs` — system prompt at line 19 defines AuraForge as "a senior engineering planning partner for software projects" that helps "clarify what they want to build so the app can later generate strong planning documents." README intro ("Turn a rough app idea into a fully scoped engineering spec") matches this intent well.

**Drift fixed in CLAUDE.md:** Portfolio-context description said "AI-assisted *creative* generation" — code and README confirm it is engineering spec/planning generation.
- Before: `Tauri 2 desktop app for AI-assisted creative generation. … Built with pnpm workspaces.`
- After: `Tauri 2 desktop app for AI-assisted engineering spec generation. … Built with npm.`

---

### 2. Current State

**Status:** `drifted` (CLAUDE.md)
**Evidence:** `src-tauri/src/lib.rs:1-13` — 10 Rust submodules registered: `artifact_diff`, `docgen`, `config`, `db`, `error`, `importer`, `lint`, `llm`, `search`, `state`, `templates`, `types`. `src-tauri/src/commands/mod.rs` — 26 registered Tauri commands covering sessions, messages, models, documents, linting, diffing, codebase import, web search, and export. `src/components/` — 20 React components including onboarding wizard, settings panel, document preview, session branching, search indicator.

**Drift fixed in CLAUDE.md:** Portfolio-context Current State said "Core Tauri scaffold with React/TypeScript frontend and Rust backend operational" — this severely understates a feature-complete application.
- Before: `Active development. Core Tauri scaffold with React/TypeScript frontend and Rust backend operational.`
- After: `Feature-complete application. Rust backend has dedicated modules for planning conversations (llm), document generation (docgen), artifact linting (lint), version diffing (artifact_diff), codebase import (importer), and proactive web search (search). SQLite persistence, configurable LLM provider (Ollama or OpenAI-compatible), and a full React frontend with onboarding wizard, session branching, document preview, and settings panel. Vitest (web) and cargo test (Rust) both configured and CI-gated.`

**Status:** `consistent` (CLAUDE.md — three documented risks) / `drifted` (README — undocumented web search privacy claim)

No data leaves your machine." — code at `src-tauri/src/config.rs:24-26` shows web search enabled by default (`enabled: true`, `proactive: true`); `src-tauri/src/commands/mod.rs:645-678` shows automatic outbound search on each user message when proactive search is on. Data does leave the machine during normal use.

**Drift fixed in README:** intro privacy claim:
- Before: `Everything runs locally via Ollama. No data leaves your machine.`
- After: `Runs locally via Ollama or any OpenAI-compatible runtime. When web search is enabled (the default), planning queries are sent to the configured search provider (DuckDuckGo by default); disable \`search.enabled\` in config for fully air-gapped use.`

Evidence basis: verified-by-reading-code

<details><summary>DOC-RECONCILIATION.md (sign-off)</summary>

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats
the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual
current state. No source code was changed and no builds or tests were run; all conclusions were
drawn by reading source files, manifests, and git history.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is
**Status: consistent**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

README and CLAUDE.md both accurately describe an API traffic interceptor that captures HTTP/S via
a browser extension or built-in MITM proxy, groups endpoints by pattern, runs Claude Sonnet
inference, and exports a Postman Collection v2.1. Core entry point confirmed at
`src-tauri/src/lib.rs` and `src/App.tsx`.

---

### 2. Current state / completion status
**Status: drifted → fixed**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

README had a WIP status badge (`status-WIP-yellow`) and a blockquote saying "AI annotation
integration in progress." The inference pipeline is fully implemented:
- `src/lib/inference.ts` — complete `runInference()` calling `claude-sonnet-4-6`
- `src-tauri/src/commands/inference.rs` — all Tauri commands wired
- `src/lib/postman-builder.ts` — complete `buildPostmanCollection()` building Collection v2.1

CLAUDE.md already correctly stated "Phases 0-4 complete."

**Changes made to README.md:**
- Badge: `status-WIP-yellow` → `status-v1.0.0-green`
- Removed blockquote "Status: Work in Progress — AI annotation integration in progress"
- Added note about setting the API key in the Settings panel (replaces the removed WIP text)

---

### 3. Stack
**Status: drifted → fixed (CLAUDE.md only)**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code — `src-tauri/Cargo.toml`, `package.json`**

Three stack entries in CLAUDE.md were wrong:

| Claim in CLAUDE.md | Actual (from manifests) | File:line |
|--------------------|-------------------------|-----------|
| `hudsucker: 0.10.x` | `hudsucker = "0.24"` | `src-tauri/Cargo.toml:31` |
| `sqlx: 0.7.x` | `rusqlite = "0.31"` (sqlx not present) | `src-tauri/Cargo.toml:23` |
| `Tailwind CSS: 3.x` | `tailwindcss: "^4"` | `package.json:27` |

An additional claim — `postman-collection (npm): 4.x — construction + validation` — was removed.
The npm package `postman-collection@4.5.0` is listed in `package.json` but is never imported in
any TypeScript source file (grep across all `.ts`/`.tsx` files returned zero matches). The actual
Postman collection is assembled from scratch in `src/lib/postman-builder.ts` using a custom type
hierarchy.

README.md's tech table already listed Tailwind CSS 4 correctly — no change needed there.

**Changes made to CLAUDE.md (both the main Tech Stack section and the mirrored
`<!-- portfolio-context -->` block):**
- `hudsucker: 0.10.x` → `0.24.x`
- `sqlx: 0.7.x — typed SQLite queries, one DB file per session` → `rusqlite: 0.31.x — SQLite via bundled feature; sessions are rows in a single apispy.db`
- `Tailwind CSS: 3.x` → `4.x`
- Removed `postman-collection (npm)` line

---

### 4. How to run
**Status: drifted → fixed (README.md)**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code — `src-tauri/src/lib.rs:63-68`, `src-tauri/src/commands/inference.rs:63-72`, `src/lib/inference.ts:123-131`**

The README Quick Start included `export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-...`. Code confirms the API key
is read via `get_setting` / `set_setting` Tauri commands backed by an SQLite `settings` table
(`src-tauri/src/db/schema.rs:84-91`); `runInference()` receives the key as a parameter pulled
from SQLite, not from an environment variable. CLAUDE.md correctly stated "Requires Anthropic API
key set in the app's settings panel (stored in SQLite, never in env files)."

The core run commands (`npm run tauri dev`, `npm run tauri build`) are confirmed valid from
`package.json:6-11`.

**Change made to README.md:**
- Removed `export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-...` from the Quick Start code block
- Added note after the tech table directing users to the in-app Settings panel

---

### 5. Storage architecture
**Status: drifted → fixed**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code — `src-tauri/src/lib.rs:47-53`**

Both README (implicitly via "session isolation" feature bullet) and CLAUDE.md Architecture section
stated: *"One SQLite `.db` file per session in `~/Library/Application Support/apispy/sessions/`"*

The actual implementation opens a **single** database file:
```rust
// src-tauri/src/lib.rs:52-53
let db_path = data_dir.join("apispy.db");
let conn = db::init_db(&db_path)...
```
Sessions are rows in the `sessions` table (`src-tauri/src/db/schema.rs:3-15`), not separate files.
The data directory is `~/Library/Application Support/apispy/`, not a `sessions/` subdirectory.

**Changes made to CLAUDE.md** (both the Architecture section and portfolio-context block):
- `One SQLite .db file per session in ~/Library/Application Support/apispy/sessions/`
  → `Single SQLite database at ~/Library/Application Support/apispy/apispy.db; each session is a row in the sessions table`

---

### 6. Known risks
**Status: consistent**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

Three listed known issues (no Safari support, Postman v2.1 only, binary body truncation) are not
contradicted by the code. `extension/chrome/` and `extension/firefox/` exist; no Safari extension
directory. No OpenAPI or Markdown export paths in any source file.

---

### 7. Next move (CLAUDE.md "Next Recommended Move")
**Status: unverifiable**
**Evidence: unverifiable-because-forward-looking**

The "Next Recommended Move" section is a project management note, not a code-verifiable claim.
Left unchanged.

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code

visualizations. `backend/detector.py` confirms multi-browser support:

brave, edge, vivaldi, and opera — matching the README's "auto-discovers Chrome, Arc, Brave,
Edge, Vivaldi, Opera, and any Chromium browser" claim. All 5 chart components
(`HeatmapCalendar.tsx`, `TopicDonut.tsx`, `DomainRanking.tsx`, `ProductivityCurve.tsx`,

`backend/categorizer.py` contains `run_ai_classification`; all launchd plists are present

**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code — `frontend/package.json`

`package.json` (`react: ^19.2.4`, `tailwindcss: 4.2.2`). Consistent; no change to README.

`CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack and Portfolio Context Stack sections said `React + TypeScript: 18 / 5.x`,
`Vite: 5.x`, `Recharts: 2.x`. Actual versions per `package.json`: React 19.2.4, Vite 8.0.1,

(Both occurrences — main Tech Stack section and Portfolio Context Stack section — updated.)

---

### 4. How to run

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code — `backend/main.py` (263 lines, no `__main__` block)

`README.md` Usage and `CLAUDE.md` Portfolio Context "How To Run" both showed:
```
cd backend && python main.py
```
`backend/main.py` has no `if __name__ == "__main__": uvicorn.run(...)` block — running
`python main.py` imports modules and exits silently without starting the server. The correct
invocation is `uvicorn main:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8000 --reload`, or `make dev` which
runs both uvicorn and Vite together (verified in `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` Makefile section).

**Changes made:**
- `README.md` Usage section: replaced `cd backend && python main.py` with `make dev` (recommended)
  plus the explicit uvicorn command for manual use.
- `CLAUDE.md` Portfolio Context "How To Run": same replacement.

---

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code

Documented constraints all hold in code: `backend/main.py:1` comment confirms API-only, no
CORS, no StaticFiles; `backend/extractor.py` opens SQLite in read-only mode (`mode=ro`);
`backend/config.py` holds all thresholds centrally (no inline literals found). No changes made.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats
the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual
current state. It changed no source code, config, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or tests.
Its purpose is to give any reviewer a traceable record of what was found, what was changed, and
what should be reviewed by a human.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is
**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `Calibrate/App/CalibrateApp.swift`, `Calibrate/Models/` (Question, DailySet, Answer,
UserProfile), `Calibrate/Views/Game/` — all confirm daily iOS prediction game with 5-question
rounds and dual confidence-interval input. README intro and CLAUDE.md overview match.

### 2. Current state (phase / features)
**Status: drifted (partially fixed)**

Two drifted items found in **README.md**:

**a. StoreKit 2 feature description was wrong.**
- File: `README.md`
- Before: `**StoreKit 2** — optional premium question packs`
- After: `**StoreKit 2 subscriptions** — monthly ($2.99) and annual ($14.99) plans unlocking premium features (calibration curve, friend groups, domain breakdown)`
- Evidence: `Calibrate/Services/PremiumStore.swift` uses `Constants.StoreKit.monthlyProductID`
  (`com.calibrate.premium.monthly`) and `Constants.StoreKit.annualProductID`
  (`com.calibrate.premium.annual`) — there are no "question packs", only subscription products.
  `project.yml` includes `Calibrate/Resources/Products.storekit`. `CLAUDE.md:38` (Key Decisions
  table) explicitly lists "Free + premium ($2.99/mo, $14.99/yr via StoreKit 2)."

**b. Global leaderboard was fully implemented but absent from the features list.**
- File: `README.md`
- Before: leaderboard not listed
- After: added `**Global leaderboard** — CloudKit-backed top-100 rankings by calibration score with personal rank display`
- Evidence: `Calibrate/Services/LeaderboardService.swift` (full CK public DB upsert + fetch),
  `Calibrate/Views/Leaderboard/LeaderboardView.swift`, `Calibrate/Views/History/CalibrationDashboardView.swift:57`
  (`leaderboardRankCard` section present in body).

Phase completion claim is **consistent**: `CLAUDE.md` says "Phase 3: Complete" which matches
`git log` entry `63c1b24 feat(phase3): complete StoreKit config, environment fixes, and settings
upgrade path` and the presence of all Phase 3 files (`FriendGroupView.swift`,
`CalibrationCurveView.swift`, `PremiumUpgradeView.swift`, `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy`).

### 3. Stack
**Status: drifted (fixed in CLAUDE.md)**

- File: `CLAUDE.md` (lines 7 and 63 — both the `## Tech Stack` section and the Portfolio Context
  `## Stack` section)
- Before: `- Language: Swift 5.10+`
- After: `- Language: Swift 6.0 (strict concurrency enabled)`
- Evidence: `project.yml:11` — `SWIFT_VERSION: "6.0"` and `project.yml:12` —
  `SWIFT_STRICT_CONCURRENCY: complete`. The README's tech table already stated "Swift 6.0
  (strict concurrency)" correctly — CLAUDE.md was the lagging copy.

All other stack items (SwiftUI iOS 17+, SwiftData, CloudKit, StoreKit 2, Swift Charts, Python CLI)
are **consistent** across README, CLAUDE.md, and code.

### 4. How to run
**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `project.yml` defines `schemes.Calibrate` with `run.config: Debug`. README
"Build and run the `Calibrate` scheme on your device or simulator from Xcode" is the correct
and only build entry point. No Makefile target overrides this for normal dev use (Makefile

**Status: consistent**

outside leaderboard/friend groups, no Claude API key in Xcode project) are all reflected in
the actual code (no `!` force-unwraps found in source; `CalibrateApp.swift` reads questions

cannot confirm or deny it — left unchanged.

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is
**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`
Entry point is `Chromafield/App/ChromafieldApp.swift`. Core modules cover Metal engine, simulation,
input, UI overlay, export, and persistence — all matching the README description of "GPU-accelerated
particle field canvas for iPhone and iPad." Four field node types (attractor, repeller, vortex,
turbulence) confirmed in `Chromafield/Metal/Shaders/SharedTypes.h:16-24` and
`Chromafield/Simulation/FieldNodeModel.swift`.

---

### 2. Current state
**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`
All 27 source files across App/, Metal/, Simulation/, Input/, UI/, Export/, Persistence/, and
Utilities/ are present and complete. Grep for TODO/FIXME/stub/fatalError found only one
`fatalError("init(coder:) is not supported")` in `Chromafield/UI/MetalCanvasView.swift:13` — the
expected `UIViewRepresentable` pattern, not a stub. Test suite has 13 test files in
`ChromafieldTests/` covering simulation correctness, behavior, device capabilities, frame budget,
persistence, export, input mapper, palette, field manager, field node model, offscreen renderer,
preset decoding, and adaptive quality — confirming the "v1.0 Feature Complete" claim.

---

### 3. Stack
**Status:** `drifted` (3 corrections applied to `CLAUDE.md`)
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

#### Drift A — Swift version
- **File:** `CLAUDE.md:7` (Tech Stack) and `CLAUDE.md:64` (portfolio-context Stack)
- **Before:** `Swift: 5.10+`
- **After:** `Swift: 6.0 (strict concurrency)`
- **Evidence:** `project.yml:11` — `SWIFT_VERSION: "6.0"` and `SWIFT_STRICT_CONCURRENCY: complete`.
  The README correctly said "Swift 6.0 (strict concurrency)" all along.

#### Drift B — Accelerate framework
- **File:** `CLAUDE.md:12` (Tech Stack) and `CLAUDE.md:69` (portfolio-context Stack)
- **Before:** `Accelerate: iOS 17+ (CPU simulation fallback only)`
- **After:** (line removed)
- **Evidence:** `grep -r "import Accelerate" Chromafield/ --include="*.swift"` returns no matches.
  Accelerate is not imported in any Swift source file; no CPU simulation fallback path exists in
  the codebase. The framework is not linked and not used.

#### Drift C — Export resolution
- **File:** `CLAUDE.md:34` (Key Decisions table)
- **Before:** `PNG: 2× screen on all devices; Video: 1× iPhone / 2× iPad`
- **After:** `PNG: 2× on M-series + A17/A18; 1× on A15/A16/unknown; Video: 2× on M-series iPad, 1× otherwise`
- **Evidence:** `Chromafield/Utilities/DeviceCapabilities.swift:46-81` — `detectParticleBudget()`
  returns `exportScalePNG: 1.0` for `case .a15, .a16, .unknown` (line 74); `exportScaleVideo` is
  1.0 for A17/A18 regardless of device form factor (line 68), and uses `isIPad ? 2.0 : 1.0` only
  for M-series chips. The "all devices" and "1× iPhone / 2× iPad" shorthand is inaccurate for
  A-series and older devices.

`README.md` stack table was already correct (`Swift 6.0 (strict concurrency)`) and did not list
Accelerate, so no README edits were needed.

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

| Task | Evidence |
|---|---|

Two tasks remain genuinely not started (no `supabase/seed.sql`, no `app/(auth)/` directory).
Deploy status is unverifiable from source.

**What was changed:**

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

**Finding B — Deprecated Supabase client API in Dev Conventions (`CLAUDE.md:34`)**

The Dev Conventions section instructed: `use createServerComponentClient in Server Components,
createRouteHandlerClient in API routes`. These are from `@supabase/auth-helpers-nextjs`, which
is not in `package.json` and is a deprecated package. The actual code at `lib/supabase/server.ts:2`
and `lib/supabase/middleware.ts:1` both import `createServerClient` from `@supabase/ssr` (`^0.8.0`),
which is the current Supabase SSR package.

**What was changed:**
- `CLAUDE.md:34` — replaced deprecated API reference with the actual one in use.

**Before:** `use createServerComponentClient in Server Components, createRouteHandlerClient in API routes`
**After:** `use createServerClient from @supabase/ssr in Server Components and API routes (see lib/supabase/)`

**Finding C — Full planned stack listed as if installed (`CLAUDE.md:6–16`)**

`CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack lists Resend, Stripe, `@react-pdf/renderer`, and the Anthropic Claude API
as part of the stack. None of these appear in `package.json`. These are the planned/target stack
for Phase 2–3, not the currently installed stack. This is a forward-looking design decision, not
a code-backed fact. **No edit made** — the "Tech Stack" section in CLAUDE.md is a product
architecture document, not an npm manifest. Marking as `unverifiable` rather than wrong, since
the section accurately describes the intended architecture.

  collision merge with momentum/mass/volume conservation in `simulation.rs:241-327`

## Contradictions for Manual Review

These are in files outside the allowed edit set. A human should apply the corrections.

### `CHANGELOG.md:9`

**What is wrong:** The entire changelog body reads `[Unreleased]: Initial release`. Multiple
features were shipped before freeze — `docs/CLOSEOUT.md` lists them explicitly: variable betting,
history analytics, theme switching, interruption detection, lean dev ops, GitHub Pages workflow,
production-readiness docs.

**One-line fix:** Replace `- Initial release` with entries derived from `docs/CLOSEOUT.md` under
an appropriate version header (e.g., `## [1.0.0] - 2024-XX-XX` or keep as `[Unreleased]` but
populate actual bullets from the Closeout "Shipped" list).

### `Makefile:3–19`

**What is wrong:** All five targets (`install`, `dev`, `build`, `test`, `lint`) delegate to
`npm install` / `npm run *`, but the repo has no `package.json`. These targets would fail.
The actual verify and test commands are in `.codex/verify.commands` and run `node` directly.

**One-line fix:** Either remove the Makefile targets, replace them with the canonical
`.codex/verify.commands` commands, or add a `package.json` with matching scripts.

### 4. How to run

**Status:** consistent  
**Evidence:** `package.json` scripts confirm `"dev": "vite"`, `"test": "vitest run"`, `"tauri": "tauri"`.
`npm run tauri dev`, `npm test`, and `npm run tauri build` all map to defined scripts.

### 5. Implemented features vs. documentation

**Status:** drifted — three corrections plus four undocumented features added  
**Evidence:**

**Correction 1 — annotation tool count:**  
README said "4 annotation tools". Actual: `src/types/index.ts:3` defines
`AnnotationTool = 'arrow' | 'rectangle' | 'text' | 'freehand' | 'redact'` (5 types).
`src/components/Toolbar.tsx:84–90` renders a "Redact" button in the tools panel.
`RedactAnnotation` (`src/types/index.ts:43–50`) supports three styles: blur, pixelate, blackbox.  
→ Changed "4 annotation tools" to "5 annotation tools"; added Redact.

**Correction 2 — OCR purpose:**  
README said "OCR via Tesseract.js extracts text from screenshots for searchable history".
Actual: `src/hooks/useOCR.ts` exports only `detectPii` — OCR maps recognized words to bounding
boxes and runs `findAllPii` (`src/lib/pii-patterns.ts`) to find emails, phone numbers, IPs, and
credit card numbers. History search (`src-tauri/src/history.rs:123–133`) filters only on
`ticket_id` and `created_at`, not OCR-extracted text.  
→ Rewrote PNG-export and OCR bullets to accurately describe PII detection.

**Correction 3 — history search scope:**  
README said "searchable history" without specifying what the search covers.
Code at `src/components/HistoryGallery.tsx:88–95` shows the search placeholder reads
"Search by ticket ID or date..." which matches `history.rs:127–133`.  
→ Added "(search by ticket ID or date)" to the thumbnail gallery bullet.

**Undocumented feature 1 — PII detection & redaction:**  
`src/components/RedactionPreview.tsx`, `src/lib/pii-patterns.ts`, `src/hooks/useOCR.ts`,
`src/App.tsx:128–181`. Full flow: OCR → PII match → region highlight → user selects →
redaction annotation added with chosen style (blur/pixelate/blackbox).  
→ Added "PII detection" bullet to Features.

**Undocumented feature 2 — upload wizard:**  
`src/components/UploadWizard.tsx`, `src-tauri/src/upload.rs` (`upload_screenshot`,
`validate_credentials` commands), `src-tauri/Cargo.toml` `reqwest` and `keyring` deps.
After saving, the app prompts to upload to a ticket; credentials stored in macOS Keychain.  
→ Added "Upload wizard" bullet to Features.

**Undocumented feature 3 — annotation templates:**  
`src/lib/templates.ts` defines 3 built-ins (`error-highlight`, `click-here`, `step-by-step`)
with relative coordinate annotations. `src/components/Toolbar.tsx:94–116` renders a
template selector dropdown.  
→ Added "Annotation templates" bullet to Features.

**Undocumented feature 4 — settings panel:**  
`src/components/SettingsPanel.tsx` exists and is rendered from both idle and annotating modes
(`src/App.tsx:274–279`, `354–360`). Content details not read to avoid scope creep; presence confirmed.  
→ Not added to Features (Settings panel is expected table-stakes for a desktop app; adding it
would raise more questions than it answers without knowing what settings are exposed. Flagged here
for a human to decide whether to document.)

**Changes:** `README.md` — Features section revised.

---

### 6. Architecture

**Status:** drifted — canvas description corrected  
**Evidence:** README described "a layered HTML5 Canvas: a base layer holds the captured screenshot
bitmap, a draw layer accumulates completed annotations as Path2D objects". Actual implementation in
`src/components/AnnotationCanvas.tsx:52,291–321`: an `<img>` element for the screenshot (absolute-
positioned) with an `<svg>` overlay. All annotation primitives are SVG elements — `<line>`,
`<polygon>`, `<rect>`, `<path>`, `<text>`. No `<canvas>` element, no `getContext('2d')`, no
`Path2D` objects anywhere in the codebase. The Tesseract.js Web Worker claim and the flat-memory
undo-stack claim are accurate.  
→ Replaced the canvas description paragraph in `README.md` Architecture section.

**Changes:** `README.md` — Architecture paragraph rewritten to describe SVG overlay.

---

None. All drifted claims were in README.md, which is an editable doc file.

 ## Architecture
 
-The annotation canvas is a layered HTML5 Canvas: a base layer holds the captured screenshot bitmap, a draw layer accumulates completed annotations as Path2D objects, and a preview layer renders the in-progress stroke. The undo stack stores serialized annotation commands, not pixel snapshots — so memory overhead stays flat regardless of image size. The Rust backend handles the macOS screenshot capture API and file I/O; Tesseract.js OCR runs in a Web Worker to avoid blocking annotation interactions.
+The annotation canvas is an `<img>` element (the screenshot) with a transparent SVG overlay. Completed and in-progress annotations are SVG primitives — `<line>`/`<polygon>` for arrows, `<rect>` for rectangles and redaction boxes, `<path>` for freehand strokes, `<text>` for labels. The undo stack stores snapshots of the annotation array, not pixel data — memory overhead stays flat regardless of image size. The Rust backend handles macOS screenshot capture and file I/O; Tesseract.js OCR runs in a Web Worker for PII detection.

(`README.md` and `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md`).

One nuance worth a human eye: the README Usage section says "Grant accessibility permissions when
prompted (required for paste injection)." This is accurate — `SnippetLibraryApp.swift:51-56` does
call `AXIsProcessTrustedWithOptions`. However, the app also requests a second permission —
**Input Monitoring** — via `HotkeyService.requestPermissions()` (`SnippetLibraryApp.swift:49`),
which is separately needed for the event tap that detects `Cmd+Shift+Space`. A user following the
README may not realise they need to grant two distinct permissions in System Settings. The
statement is not wrong, just incomplete. Consider adding "and Input Monitoring permissions" to the
Usage sentence. (This pass left it unchanged because the existing text is not false.)

code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual
current state. No source code, config, tests, or lockfiles were modified, and no builds or tests

### 1. What it is

(Leaflet heatmap, Recharts charts, vis-network graph, FastAPI sidecar at localhost:8008).
`sidecar/main.py` confirms FastAPI + APScheduler + SQLite backend.

---

### 2. Current state
**Status:** `drifted` — fixed in `CLAUDE.md`

**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code` — All 5 visualization components exist and are
non-stub: `src/components/geo-heatmap.tsx`, `skill-bar-chart.tsx`, `salary-box-plot.tsx`,
`co-occurrence-graph.tsx`, `trend-lines.tsx`. All sidecar services are present:
`sidecar/services/adzuna_client.py`, `nlp_pipeline.py`, `role_normalizer.py`,
`salary_resolver.py`, `sync_orchestrator.py`. All API routers exist:
`sidecar/routers/{geo,jobs,salaries,skills,sync,trends,credentials}.py`. Tests exist at
`sidecar/tests/`. Filter persistence is implemented in `src/App.tsx:67-96` via
tauri-plugin-store. `src-tauri/binaries/main-aarch64-apple-darwin` is present. The
PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION (`docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md`) explicitly calls out the memory drift:
"architectural backbone shipped" well beyond Phase 0.

**Changes made:**
- `CLAUDE.md` — "Current Phase" (top section):
  `Phase 0: Foundation` → `Phases 0–2 complete (scaffold, ingestion pipeline, 5 visualizations + filter panel). Release-closeout cadence (v1.0 bump, CSP hardening, baseline Rust tests, .dmg packaging) not yet started.`
- `CLAUDE.md` — "Current State" (portfolio-context block):
  Same change as above.

---

### 3. Stack
**Status:** `drifted` — fixed in `CLAUDE.md`

**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

| Library | Documented | Actual | Source |
|---|---|---|---|
| Recharts | 2 | 3.8.0 | `package.json:21` |
| vis-network | 9 | 10.0.2 | `package.json:23` |
| APScheduler | 3.10 | 3.11.2 | `sidecar/requirements.txt:9` |
| Credential storage | "macOS Keychain via keytar" | `tauri-plugin-store` file store (`credentials.json`) | `src-tauri/src/lib.rs:16-18`, `sidecar/core/credentials.py` |

`keytar` is not imported or depended on anywhere in the codebase. `tauri-plugin-store` is the
actual mechanism used (`src-tauri/Cargo.toml:21`). Credentials are written to a store file named
`credentials.json` and hydrated to the sidecar as in-memory Python variables at startup
(`src/App.tsx:80-89`, `sidecar/core/credentials.py`).

**Changes made:**
- `CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack (top): `Recharts 2` → `Recharts 3`; `vis-network 9` → `vis-network 10`; `APScheduler 3.10` → `APScheduler 3.11`; `keytar (Rust tauri-plugin-store) — API key storage in macOS Keychain, never plaintext` → `tauri-plugin-store — API key storage via Tauri store (credentials.json in app data dir); hydrated to sidecar memory at startup`
- `CLAUDE.md` Stack (portfolio-context block): same four changes.

---

### 4. How to run
**Status:** `drifted` — fixed in `README.md`

**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code` — README installation block referenced
`./src-python` (`README.md:27`) but no such directory exists; the Python backend is in
`sidecar/` with a `requirements.txt` (`sidecar/requirements.txt:1`). There is no `setup.py` or
`pyproject.toml` in `sidecar/`, so `-e` (editable install) would fail.

**Change made:**
- `README.md:27`: `pip install -e ./src-python` → `pip install -r sidecar/requirements.txt`

The `pnpm tauri dev` command is consistent with `package.json:8`.

---

### 5. Known risks / security
**Status:** `unverifiable` (partial)

`tauri-plugin-store` on macOS writes to a JSON file in the app data directory
(`~/Library/Application Support/<app-name>/`), not the OS Keychain. Whether the store
plugin is configured for Keychain-backed encryption vs. plaintext JSON cannot be confirmed by
reading the source alone (it depends on how the store is opened and whether platform-specific
encryption is enabled). The documentation previously called this "macOS Keychain via keytar"
— that was inaccurate (keytar is absent from the codebase). The corrected wording in CLAUDE.md
now accurately describes the mechanism; whether the store file is encrypted at rest is
`unverifiable-because-requires-runtime-inspection`. PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION already flags this
for operator verification (`docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md:159`).

---

### 6. Next move
**Status:** `consistent` (after phase-status fix above)

The PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION (`docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md:140-157`) accurately describes the
next moves: branch consolidation, v1.0 release-closeout cadence, Python sidecar packaging
verification, and APScheduler-when-closed posture decision. These are `consistent` with the
actual code state (no release-closeout artifacts: no v1.0.0 tag, no CSP in
`src-tauri/capabilities/default.json`, no baseline Rust tests). Now that CLAUDE.md's phase
claim is corrected, that doc also points to this next arc.

---

(`npm install recharts tailwindcss autoprefixer postcss nanoid`).

is not installed and not in `package.json`.

**One-line fix:** Remove `nanoid` from the install command; note in the text that IDs use
`crypto.randomUUID()`.

### 1. What It Is

and iPad, 7 spaces, no HUD, SceneKit + Metal, $4.99 premium. Code confirms:
- All 7 `SpaceRule` implementations present (`DopplerRule`, `LensingRule`, `ShadowRule`,
  `InterferenceRule`, `ChromaticDecayRule`, `ResonanceRule`, `ConvergenceRule`).

- All 7 Metal shaders present in `Liminal/Shaders/` (`Doppler.metal`, `Lensing.metal`,
  `Shadow.metal`, `Interference.metal`, `ChromaticDecay.metal`, `Resonance.metal`,
  `Convergence.metal`, `ConvergenceGeometry.metal`, `ResonanceGeometry.metal`,
  `Common.metal`).
- All 7 rule types implemented (`Liminal/Spaces/Rules/`).
- `SpaceScene.swift`, `SpaceViewController.swift`, `TitleScene.swift`,
  `TransitionManager.swift` all fully implemented.
- `HapticManager.swift` present; 5-tap hidden settings panel wired in
  `SpaceViewController`.
- 11 test files in `LiminalTests/` (one per rule + top-level tests), far beyond the 3
  described in Phase 0's acceptance criteria.
- Git log contains 7+ App Store prep commits (signing, icons, privacy policy,
  DEVELOPMENT_TEAM, Privacy Manifest, ExportOptions, app icon).
- `APPSTORE-METADATA.md` has a full submission checklist.
- `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` explicitly states: "feature-complete; all phases done"
  and classifies the repo as "Release Frozen (iOS App Store, paid)".

**Changes made to `CLAUDE.md`:**
- `## Current Phase` (main body): "Phase 0: Foundation + ShaderLab (Weeks 1–2)" →
  "Feature-complete — all 5 phases shipped; App Store submission ready"
- `## Current State` (Portfolio Context): same substitution

---

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

README Tech Stack table and CLAUDE.md both list Swift 6.0, SceneKit, Metal, AVAudioEngine,
SpriteKit, CoreHaptics, Xcode 16.x. All confirmed:
- `LiminalApp.swift` and `AppDelegate.swift` confirm UIKit/SwiftUI lifecycle + AVAudioSession.
- `.metal` files confirm Metal GPU usage.
- `AudioManager.swift` confirms AVAudioEngine.
- `TitleScene.swift` confirms SpriteKit for title only.
- `HapticManager.swift` confirms CoreHaptics.
- No `Package.swift` or third-party imports found anywhere.

No changes made.

---

### 4. How to Run (Controls)

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

Both `README.md` (Quick Start → Usage) and `CLAUDE.md` (Portfolio Context → How To Run)
stated: "Swipe to move, tilt to look."

This is wrong on two counts. `PlayerController.swift` wires three gestures:
- `handleLookPan` (`UIPanGestureRecognizer`, 1 touch) → rotates camera (drag, not tilt)
- `handleMovePan` (`UIPanGestureRecognizer`, 2 touches) → translates camera
- `handlePinch` (`UIPinchGestureRecognizer`) → speed multiplier 0.5×–3.0×

There is no gyroscope/accelerometer tilt input anywhere in the codebase. The verifiably
correct description (also matching `APPSTORE-METADATA.md`) is drag-to-look, two-finger
drag-to-move, pinch-to-speed.

**Changes made:**
- `README.md` line 31: "Swipe to move, tilt to look." →
  "Drag to look, two-finger drag to move, pinch to adjust speed."
- `CLAUDE.md` (Portfolio Context → How To Run): same substitution

---

### 5. Architecture Description

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

`README.md` Architecture paragraph contained three inaccurate claims:

**a) "SpaceLoader compiles the associated Metal shader into a `SCNProgram`"**
`SpaceLoader.swift` is a pure JSON decoder — it never touches shaders. The shader is
attached in `SpaceScene.createShaderMaterial()` via `material.shaderModifiers =
[.fragment: source]` (SCNShaderModifierEntryPoint), not `SCNProgram`. CLAUDE.md's "Key
Decisions" table and "Do NOT" list both explicitly prohibit `SCNProgram`; this was a
stale/aspirational description that never matched the implementation.

**b) "RuleEngine runs on CADisplayLink"**
`RuleEngine.evaluate` is called from `SpaceViewController.renderer(_:updateAtTime:)`, the
`SCNSceneRendererDelegate` callback — not a standalone `CADisplayLink`. (`CADisplayLink`
is used explicitly only in `ShaderLabViewController` in the separate `LiminalShaderLab`
target.)

**c) "writes a `simd_float4x4` uniform buffer"**
`RuleOutput.shaderUniforms` is `[String: Float]`. `ShaderUniformBus.update(_:uniforms:)`
pushes each entry via `material.setValue(value, forKey: key)`. No `simd_float4x4`
anywhere in the uniform path.

**Change made to `README.md` Architecture paragraph:**
Old: "At runtime, the `SpaceLoader` compiles the associated Metal shader into a `SCNProgram`
and attaches it to the scene graph. The `RuleEngine` runs on `CADisplayLink` and writes a
`simd_float4x4` uniform buffer that both the Metal shader and the AVAudioEngine parameter
automation consume on the same tick…"

New: "At runtime, `SpaceScene` loads the Metal shader by name and attaches it as an
`SCNShaderModifierEntryPointFragment` on the space material, keeping SceneKit's lighting
pass intact. The `RuleEngine` is driven by `SCNSceneRendererDelegate.renderer(_:updateAtTime:)`
each frame and produces a `[String: Float]` uniform dictionary that `ShaderUniformBus`
pushes to the material via `setValue(_:forKey:)`; the same `RuleOutput` simultaneously
drives AVAudioEngine parameter updates…"

---

### 6. Known Risks / Constraints

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

CLAUDE.md's "Key Decisions" table and "Do NOT" list describe constraints that the code
respects: shader modifiers (not `SCNProgram`), JSON-driven parameters (no hardcoded floats
in Swift), no third-party Swift packages, no in-game UI. All confirmed by reading the
production source.

No changes made.

The implementation IS complete (the `update` method is fully functional). This is a stale

The `RuleEngine` is driven by `SCNSceneRendererDelegate.renderer(_:updateAtTime:)` each frame and produces a `[String: Float]` uniform dictionary that `ShaderUniformBus` pushes to the material via `setValue(_:forKey:)`; the same `RuleOutput` simultaneously drives AVAudioEngine parameter updates, keeping visuals and audio synchronized without a separate message-passing step.

## Per-claim findings

### 1. What it is

**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `src-tauri/src/main.rs`, `src-tauri/Cargo.toml`, `src/App.tsx`, `package.json` all
confirm a Tauri 2 macOS desktop app with a Rust packet engine and React/TypeScript frontend.
README description and CLAUDE.md intro match. No edits made.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status: drifted → fixed**

Two false claims in `README.md` and one false claim in `CLAUDE.md`.

**README.md — status badge (line 3)**
- Before: `status-WIP-yellow`
- After: `status-v1.0.0-green`
- Evidence: `package.json` version `"1.0.0"`, `src-tauri/Cargo.toml` version `"1.0.0"`,
  `export_pcap` command fully implemented at `src-tauri/src/commands.rs:77-105`,
  live capture implemented at `src-tauri/src/commands.rs:25-31`.

**README.md — status blurb (line 39)**
- Before: `**Status: Work in Progress** — Core decoding and all three views functional on macOS. PCAP export and live-capture UI in progress.`
- After: `**Status: v1.0.0** — All phases complete. Live capture, PCAP import/export, and all three view modes fully implemented.`
- Evidence: same as above; `export_pcap` and `start_capture`/`stop_capture` all present and
  non-stub in `commands.rs`. `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` also confirms "v1.0.0" and
  "Phases 0-4 complete in single feat commit."

**CLAUDE.md — QUIC decoder claim (line 19, and portfolio-context block)**
- Before: `Protocol decoders: HTTP, DNS, TLS (handshake metadata), QUIC`
- After: `Protocol decoders: HTTP, DNS, TLS (handshake metadata)`
- Evidence: `src-tauri/src/parser/types.rs` `LayerData` enum contains `Http`, `Dns`, `Tls`,
  `Raw` — no `Quic` variant. `TopProtocol` enum has no `Quic` variant.
  `src-tauri/src/parser/application.rs` implements `try_parse_http`, `try_parse_dns`,
  `try_parse_tls` — no QUIC parser. Ripgrep over all Rust source files finds no `quic` or
  `QUIC` string. The claim was never implemented.

---

### 3. Stack

**Status: drifted → fixed**

`CLAUDE.md` listed four frontend dependency version families that did not match `package.json`.

| Dependency | CLAUDE.md (before) | `package.json` (actual) | CLAUDE.md (after) |
|---|---|---|---|
| React | 18.x | `^19.1.0` | 19.x |
| Zustand | 4.x | `5.0.12` | 5.x |
| Tailwind CSS | 3.x | `4.2.2` | 4.x |
| Vite | 5.x | `^7.0.4` | 7.x |

The same four version lines appear verbatim in both the main Tech Stack section and inside the
`<!-- portfolio-context -->` block; both occurrences were corrected in the same edit.

Remaining stack entries are consistent: TypeScript ~5.8 (`package.json`) matches "5.x";
`@tanstack/react-virtual` 3.13 matches "3.x"; Tauri 2 matches Cargo.toml; `pcap = "2"` and
`pnet = "0.35"` match Cargo.toml exactly.

---

### 4. How to run

**Status: consistent**
`npm install` and `npm run tauri dev` / `npm run tauri build` are present as scripts in
`package.json:6-11`. libpcap dependency note and capture-privilege note match the code's actual
requirements. No edits made.

---

### 5. Known risks / limitations

**Status: consistent**
CLAUDE.md notes "TLS payload decryption not supported" and "Privilege escalation UX for live
capture may require manual permissions." Both are accurate: `src-tauri/src/parser/application.rs`
parses only TLS handshake metadata (ClientHello/ServerHello), never decrypts payload. Live
capture privilege flow is noted in code comments. No edits made.

---

### 6. Next move

**Status: unverifiable**
"Next Recommended Move" in CLAUDE.md is a forward-looking suggestion ("resume the next active
task, promote the repo…"). Cannot be verified from code alone. Left unchanged.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass. The pass treats the
source code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it accurately reflects the
repository's actual current state. No source code was modified and no builds or tests were executed —
all evidence was gathered by reading manifests, source files, test files, and git history.

---

## Per-claim findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

README intro, CLAUDE.md summary, and AGENTS.md project goal all accurately describe a zero-backend,
in-browser neural network playground built with TensorFlow.js. Entry point is `src/app/page.tsx`
(Next.js App Router). Core modules — `src/workers/training.worker.ts`, `src/lib/model-compiler.ts`,
`src/lib/dataset-loader.ts`, `src/stores/` — match the described architecture. No code was found
that contradicts the "zero-backend, client-side only" claim.

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

CLAUDE.md and AGENTS.md both declare Phase 3 complete. All components listed in the Phase 3 scope
are implemented: `src/lib/url-state.ts` (URL sharing via LZ-string), `src/constants/tutorials.ts`
(3 tutorial objects), all playground UI components under `src/components/playground/`. The project
is deployed (Vercel URL present in `src/app/layout.tsx`). The CIFAR-10 dataset files are gitignored
(referenced in AGENTS.md and CLAUDE.md). No stubs, TODOs, or roadmap items were found that
contradict the "Phase 3 complete" claim.

### 3. Stack — versions

**Status:** `drifted` (Next.js version, React version)
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

- **Next.js:** `package.json` declares `"next": "15.5.15"`. README (badge + 2 tech-table rows) and
  CLAUDE.md (2 places: Tech Stack + Portfolio Context Stack) all said "14". Fixed.
  - `README.md`: badge `Next.js%2014` → `Next.js%2015`; tech highlights table `Next.js 14` ×2 → `Next.js 15` ×2; tech stack table `Next.js 14` → `Next.js 15`
  - `CLAUDE.md`: `**Next.js**: 14+` → `**Next.js**: 15+` (fixed in both the Tech Stack and Stack sections)

- **React:** `package.json` declares `"react": "^19.2.5"`. CLAUDE.md (2 places) said "18+". Fixed.
  - `CLAUDE.md`: `**React**: 18+` → `**React**: 19+` (fixed in both the Tech Stack and Stack sections)

- All other versions (TF.js 4.x, Zustand 4.x, D3 7.x, Comlink 4.x, idb-keyval 6.x, Tailwind 3.x,
  TypeScript 5.x) match `package.json` exactly. No changes needed.

### 4. How to run

**Status:** `drifted` (package manager)
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

README's "Running locally" and "Building for production" sections used `pnpm install`, `pnpm dev`,
and `pnpm build` exclusively. Both `package-lock.json` (npm) and `pnpm-lock.yaml` coexist in the
repo. CLAUDE.md's `Build & Run` section and AGENTS.md's canonical verification commands both use
`npm` (`npm install`, `npm run dev`, `npm ci`, etc.), indicating npm is at minimum equally canonical.
The README was updated to show both: `npm install   # or: pnpm install` and
`npm run dev   # or: pnpm dev`, and `npm run build   # or: pnpm build`.

CLAUDE.md architecture paths were also corrected:
- `lib/worker/` → `src/workers/` (actual path from Glob)
- `lib/stores/` → `src/stores/`
- `lib/types.ts` → `src/types/index.ts`

### 5. Known risks

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

All three documented risks match reality:
- CIFAR-10 binary files are gitignored (confirmed by their absence from the Glob result).
- Input layer compressed representation is in `src/lib/network-layout.ts` and referenced in `src/components/playground/NetworkCanvas.tsx`.
- WebGPU fallback chain (WebGPU → WebGL → WASM) is implemented in `src/lib/backend-selector.ts`.

### 6. Next move

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `unverifiable-because-forward-looking`

CLAUDE.md and AGENTS.md describe "promote the repo beyond minimum-viable" as the next recommended
move after Phase 3. Nothing in the code contradicts this. No active stubs or failing roadmap items
were found that would imply a different next step.

## Contradictions for manual review

These involve files outside the editable set (`README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`,
`DOC-RECONCILIATION.md`, `docs/`). They should not be edited by the reconciliation pass; a human
should apply the fix.

### 1. `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` — analytics claim

`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` Security section (line 334) states:
> "No telemetry, no analytics, no external API calls."

But `package.json` lists `"@vercel/analytics": "^2.0.1"` as a dependency, and `src/app/layout.tsx`
line 1 imports and renders `<Analytics />` from `@vercel/analytics/react`.

**One-line fix:** Remove or update the "no analytics" claim in `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:334` to
acknowledge the Vercel Analytics integration added post-roadmap.

### 2. `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` — Vercel deployment URL

`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` Phase 3 Task 9 (line 470) gives the expected Vercel URL as
`neural-network-playground.vercel.app`. The actual URL in `src/app/layout.tsx:6` is
`https://neural-network-playground-delta.vercel.app`.

**One-line fix:** Update `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:470` to reflect the actual deployed URL
(`neural-network-playground-delta.vercel.app`).

### 3. `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` — CIFAR-10 dataset size

`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` Phase 2 Task 7 (line 431) describes a "60MB download" warning for
CIFAR-10. `src/constants/datasets.ts:52` records `downloadSizeMB: 30`, and README's dataset table
also says 30 MB. The roadmap figure (60 MB) is stale.

**One-line fix:** Update `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:431` "60MB download" to "30MB download".

the committed tree at that commit and at current HEAD. The following edits were made:

- Removed `launchd/` and `nginx/` from the verified tree listing; added a note that they are absent
- Updated the "Why self-hosted service" rationale to rely on the daemon model rather than absent deploy configs
- Updated the "Distribution model" table row to remove the `launchd + nginx` claim
- Updated the "Deploy config" table row to note configs are not committed
- Updated the "self-hosted service cluster" cluster definition to list deploy configs as future candidate signals rather than existing evidence
- Updated the reactivation procedure: replaced "audit launchd/ and nginx/ configs" with a note that they need to be authored

<details><summary>DOC-RECONCILIATION.md (sign-off)</summary>

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current state. It changed no source code, configuration, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or test commands — all evidence was gathered by reading source, manifest, and test files. This file exists so the pass is auditable and future contributors can see what was verified and what remains uncertain.

---

## Per-claim findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** consistent  
**Evidence:** `README.md:3`, `AGENTS.md:5-8`, `app/(product)/dashboard/page.tsx:11`, `lib/navigation.ts:1-79`  
The product description ("private-first career evidence ledger for collecting proof of real work, reviewing it deliberately, and generating traceable resume or changelog drafts only from approved evidence") is confirmed by the navigation definition, dashboard copy, and domain contracts in `docs/DOMAIN.md` and `docs/TRUST-GUARDRAILS.md`.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status:** consistent  
**Evidence:** `docs/PHASE_STATUS.md`, `app/(product)/dashboard/page.tsx:70-71`, `lib/navigation.ts:18-79`, `app/api/exports/route.ts`, `app/api/exports/[id]/route.ts`, `app/(product)/exports/page.tsx`, `app/(product)/review-cycle/page.tsx`, test files `tests/unit/export-contracts.test.ts`, `tests/unit/export-serializers.test.ts`, `tests/unit/review-cycle-logic.test.ts`, `tests/integration/export-create-route.test.ts`, `tests/integration/export-download-route.test.ts`, `tests/e2e/exports-review-cycle.spec.ts`

All Milestone 7 routes (`/exports`, `/review-cycle`) and APIs (`POST /api/exports`, `GET /api/exports/:id`) are present in code. The test suite (26 unit + integration test files and 5 e2e spec files) covers all seven milestones. Dashboard hard-codes "Milestone 7 complete" and "The v1 roadmap is complete through Milestone 7." README and `docs/PHASE_STATUS.md` are accurate.

---

### 3. Stack

**Status:** drifted (in AGENTS.md portfolio-context block only)  
**Evidence:** `package.json:5` (all scripts use `pnpm`), `AGENTS.md:157`, `.codex/verify.commands:4`  
**What changed:** `AGENTS.md` — portfolio-context Stack line  
Before → After: `- JavaScript package manager: npm-compatible workflow` → `- JavaScript package manager: pnpm`

The rest of the stack description is consistent: Next.js 16.2.3, TypeScript, Supabase SSR 0.10.2 + supabase-js 2.103.0, OpenAI 6.34.0, Zod 4.3.6, Vitest 4.1.4, and Playwright 1.59.1 are all confirmed in `package.json`. Note: the Supabase key env var in the codebase is `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY` (confirmed at `lib/env.ts:7` and `lib/supabase/server.ts:11`) — the new Supabase v2 name, not the older `ANON_KEY`. No doc explicitly names this key wrong (no doc names it at all), so no additional edit is needed.

---

### 4. How to run

**Status:** consistent  
**Evidence:** `package.json:5-18`, `README.md:61-66`, `AGENTS.md:48-56`, `.codex/verify.commands`

Every command the README documents — `pnpm dev`, `pnpm check`, `pnpm db:reset`, `pnpm db:test`, `pnpm test:e2e`, `pnpm build` — is defined in `package.json` scripts. The `.codex/verify.commands` file is consistent with AGENTS.md's verifier contract.

One item unverifiable: README step 2 says `cp .env.example .env.local` (`README.md:15`). The `.env.example` file could not be confirmed to exist through available read tools (Glob returned no results; direct Read returned a tool permission error). If the file is missing, the setup instruction will silently fail for new contributors. **Marked unverifiable** — a human should confirm the file is tracked in git.

---

### 5. Known risks / contradictions

**Status:** drifted (README omits a live product route)  
**Evidence:** `lib/navigation.ts:26-30`, `app/(product)/inbox/page.tsx`, `lib/evidence/queries.ts` (referenced from inbox page)  
**What changed:** `README.md` — routes description paragraph  
Before → After: `GitHub import runs from `/github`.` → `Evidence capture runs from `/inbox`. GitHub import runs from `/github`.`

`/inbox` is a fully implemented, auth-protected product route registered in the primary navigation as "Fast evidence capture" from Milestone 2. It loads real evidence data via `listRecentEditableEvidence`. The README called out `/github`, `/exports`, and `/review-cycle` by URL but silently omitted `/inbox`. A reader following the README alone would have no indication that the primary capture surface exists.

---

### 6. Next move

| Error | Evidence | Correction |

| "The Rust backend handles all SQLite writes" | `src/lib/db.ts` — all SQL queries originate in frontend JS via `tauri-plugin-sql`; Rust handles keychain + launchd only | "The Rust backend handles keychain operations … and registers the launchd agent; SQLite reads and writes flow through `tauri-plugin-sql` from the frontend." |

| "streams field suggestions back" | `src/lib/receipt-parser.ts:116-163` — `client.messages.create()` (blocking); no streaming | "the response is structured JSON" |

| "lightweight Rust binary (bundled in the app)" | `src-tauri/src/commands/notifications.rs:28,31` — plist `ProgramArguments` points to `env::current_exe()` (the main app binary) with `--check-notifications` | "re-invokes the main app binary with `--check-notifications`" |
| "just a scheduled job that runs at login" | `src-tauri/src/commands/notifications.rs:46-53` — plist has both `RunAtLoad=true` and `StartCalendarInterval {Hour=9, Minute=0}` | "runs at 9 AM daily and on each login" |

 ## Architecture
 
-The Rust backend handles all SQLite writes and the launchd agent registration for background deadline checks. Receipt parsing is fire-and-forget: the frontend sends raw receipt text to a Tauri command that calls the Anthropic API and streams field suggestions back. The launchd agent runs a lightweight Rust binary (bundled in the app) that queries SQLite and fires `osascript` notifications — no daemon, no background process, just a scheduled job that runs at login.
+The Rust backend handles keychain operations (storing and retrieving the Anthropic API key) and registers the launchd agent; SQLite reads and writes flow through `tauri-plugin-sql` from the frontend. Receipt parsing sends a receipt image to Claude directly from the frontend JavaScript layer — the API key is fetched from macOS Keychain via `invoke("get_api_key")` before the Anthropic SDK call; the response is structured JSON that pre-fills the purchase form. The launchd agent re-invokes the main app binary with `--check-notifications`; that headless Rust path opens SQLite with sqlx, fires native notifications via `notify_rust` for 7-day and 1-day deadlines, and records each firing in `notification_log` to prevent duplicates — the agent runs at 9 AM daily and on each login.

## Contradictions for Manual Review

### docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md — microphone claim (fixed in docs/ per edit rules)

`docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` described the app as using "**microphone capture** to measure the room's acoustic response." The codebase contains no microphone usage whatsoever:
- `grep -r "microphone|AVCapture|NSMicrophoneUsage" RoomTone/` → no matches
- `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md` Security section explicitly states: "**No microphone.** All audio is synthesized. `NSMicrophoneUsageDescription` must NOT be added."
- `PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy` declares only `NSPrivacyAccessedAPICategoryUserDefaults` — no microphone entry.

This was a factual error in `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` (a file I am allowed to edit). Fixed in three locations:
- "Current state" paragraph: removed "microphone capture" language
- Unblock trigger item #3: removed `NSMicrophoneUsageDescription` task, replaced with a note not to add it; renumbered items 4–7 → 3–6
- Portfolio operating system table: replaced "Microphone usage description clarity" row with a note that no microphone is used

### project.yml:38 — bundle ID typo (code file, cannot edit)

`project.yml:38` sets `PRODUCT_BUNDLE_IDENTIFIER: com.romtone.app` (missing first 'o' — "romtone" not "roomtone"). `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md:152` records the Bundle ID as `com.roomtone.app`.

One of these is wrong. The App Store Connect record determines which is authoritative. A human must reconcile the `project.yml` typo against the App Store Connect bundle ID before submission.

**Fix:** If the App Store Connect record uses `com.roomtone.app`, correct `project.yml:38` and `project.yml:57` (tests target) to match. If ASC uses `com.romtone.app`, update `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md:152` accordingly.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current state. It changed no source code, config, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or tests. Its purpose is to give reviewers an auditable record of what was verified, what was corrected, and what remains for a human to address.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `src/manifest.ts`, `src/background/service-worker.ts`, `src/content/overlay.ts`, `src/content/dom-extractor.ts`. The README and CLAUDE.md descriptions — Chrome MV3 extension, region selection, DOM-first extraction with Vision fallback, four export formats, extraction history — all match the implemented code.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** All four phases are implemented. Phase 0: `src/manifest.ts`, `src/lib/storage.ts`, `src/popup/components/Settings.tsx`. Phase 1: `src/background/service-worker.ts` (full extraction pipeline), `src/offscreen/offscreen.ts`, `src/lib/api.ts`. Phase 2: `src/lib/parser.ts`, `src/popup/components/History.tsx`, `src/popup/components/ExportBar.tsx`; keyboard shortcut registered in `src/manifest.ts:34-41`; context menu wired in `src/background/service-worker.ts:356-368`. Phase 3: `src/content/dom-extractor.ts`, `src/lib/cost.ts`, chart mode in `src/lib/api.ts:46`.

---

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `drifted` (one item) — fixed in `CLAUDE.md`

`CLAUDE.md` listed `@anthropic-ai/sdk 0.52+` in both the Tech Stack section and the Portfolio Context section. The installed version in `package.json:17` is `0.80.0`.

**Change:** `@anthropic-ai/sdk 0.52+` → `@anthropic-ai/sdk 0.80+` (two occurrences in `CLAUDE.md`). `README.md` was already version-agnostic ("Anthropic Claude Vision API") and needed no change.

---

### 4. How to run

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `package.json:6-11` defines `dev` (vite), `build` (tsc --noEmit && vite build), `test` (vitest run), `test:watch`, and `typecheck` (tsc --noEmit). Every command documented in README and CLAUDE.md exists as a named script.

---

### 5. Architecture / file paths

**Status:** `drifted` — fixed in `CLAUDE.md` and `README.md`

**Drift 1 — wrong directory name (`CLAUDE.md`):**
CLAUDE.md Architecture listed `src/service-worker/` as the message routing hub. The actual directory is `src/background/`, containing `src/background/service-worker.ts` (confirmed by glob and `src/manifest.ts:24`).
Change: `src/service-worker/` → `src/background/`

**Drift 2 — nonexistent file (`CLAUDE.md`):**
CLAUDE.md Architecture listed `src/lib/extraction.ts` for DOM-first extraction logic. No such file exists. The DOM extraction module is `src/content/dom-extractor.ts`; the Vision API wrapper is `src/lib/api.ts`.
Change: `src/lib/extraction.ts — DOM-first extraction logic; Vision API as fallback` → `src/content/dom-extractor.ts — DOM-first extraction logic; Vision API (src/lib/api.ts) as fallback`

**Drift 3 — incorrect orchestration description (`README.md`):**
README Architecture paragraph stated "If no table is found, it [the content script] crops the page screenshot and sends it to a background service worker." Screenshot capture and cropping are performed by the service worker via `chrome.tabs.captureVisibleTab()` and an offscreen document (`src/offscreen/offscreen.ts`), not by the content script. The content script only handles the selection overlay and responds to `DOM_EXTRACT_REQUEST` messages from the service worker.
Change: reworded the paragraph to correctly attribute capture/crop to the service worker and DOM extraction to the content script.

---

### 6. Known risks

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** The three documented risks — `@crxjs/vite-plugin` 2.x beta quirks, DOM-first extraction quality variance, and cost display estimation — all accurately reflect knowable concerns from the code. The beta label on `@crxjs/vite-plugin@2.4.0` is accurate (package metadata confirms beta channel). Cost estimation risk is genuine: `src/lib/cost.ts` hardcodes per-token pricing which must be kept in sync with Anthropic's rate card.

---

## Contradictions for Manual Review

The following files contain drift but are outside the editable set. A human should apply these fixes.

### `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md`

**1. Haiku pricing stale — `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:549`**
Roadmap states: `"Haiku input $0.25/MTok, output $1.25/MTok"`.
Actual pricing in `src/lib/cost.ts:4-7`: `{ input: 0.8, output: 4.0 }` ($0.80/$4.00 per MTok).
One-line fix: update the Haiku pricing row in the Phase 3 token-display description.

**2. "Deferred (v2+)" lists DOM-first as unshipped — `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:288`**
The Scope Boundaries "Deferred (v2+)" section still lists `"DOM-first hybrid extraction (try HTML parsing before vision)"` as unimplemented. This feature was shipped in Phase 3 (see `src/content/dom-extractor.ts`).
One-line fix: move or remove this item from the Deferred list, noting it was shipped in Phase 3.

**3. StorageSchema missing Phase 3 keys — `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:99-115`**
The documented `StorageSchema` interface omits four keys added in Phase 3: `settings.domFirst`, `usage.inputTokens`, `usage.outputTokens`, and `extraction.current`. These are present in `src/types/index.ts:95-107` and `src/lib/storage.ts`.
One-line fix: add the four missing keys to the roadmap's StorageSchema block.

| Error | Reality | Fixed to |
|-------|---------|----------|
| "A `DSPProcessor` actor" | Private class `PipelineState` inside `AccelerometerPipeline`; no public `DSPProcessor` type | "A private `PipelineState` object…inside `AccelerometerPipeline`" |

 ## Architecture
 
-CoreMotion pushes accelerometer samples to a ring buffer on a real-time thread. A `DSPProcessor` actor applies the filter chain and STA/LTA detection, emitting `SeismicEvent` values when threshold crossings occur. The Metal renderer reads the ring buffer directly via a shared `MTLBuffer`, avoiding any copy on the hot path. USGS correlation happens in a background `Task` with exponential backoff retries, writing results back to SwiftData where `@Query` observers in the detail view pick them up.
+CoreMotion pushes accelerometer samples into an `AccelerometerPipeline` on a background queue. A private `PipelineState` object applies the filter chain and feeds the `STALTADetector`, yielding `TriggerEvent` values via `AsyncStream`. The `EventCoordinator` actor bridges these streams to the main actor, appending magnitudes to `RibbonState.samples` and persisting `SeismicEvent` records to SwiftData on each trigger. The Metal renderer copies the current samples into a triple-buffered `MTLBuffer` each frame. USGS correlation happens in a background `Task` with exponential backoff retries, writing results back to SwiftData; `EventDetailView` fetches the updated record on appearance via `FetchDescriptor`.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which
treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the
repo's actual current state. No code was changed and no builds or tests were run. It exists
to give any reviewer a full audit trail of what was checked, what was changed, and what
requires a human's eye.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

All seven chapters are present and implemented:
- `src/chapters/the-test.ts`, `the-signal.ts`, `the-forecast.ts`, `the-update.ts`,
  `the-market.ts`, `the-evidence.ts`, `the-convergence.ts` — all exist with full configs.
- Corresponding content components (`src/components/chapter/content/The*Content.tsx`) exist
  for all seven.
- All seven chapter slugs are wired into `src/app/chapter/[slug]/page.tsx` via dynamic imports.

README description, CLAUDE.md overview, and AGENTS.md project goal all accurately describe
the project as a seven-chapter interactive Bayesian reasoning essay. No changes made.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent` (with one implementation gap noted below)
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

Docs claim "v1.0.0 — Complete, All 7 chapters implemented and playable." Code confirms:
- All 7 chapter config files, visualization components, and content components exist.
- 11 Vitest test files present across `src/chapters/` and `src/lib/`.
- 1 Playwright E2E smoke test at `e2e/smoke.spec.ts`.
- `package.json` version is `1.0.0`.

**Implementation gap (not changing, flagged below):** `src/app/chapter/[slug]/page.tsx:51`
references `/og/${chapter.slug}.png` for OpenGraph images, but `public/og/` does not exist —
no OG image files were created. The docs describe the architectural decision (static PNGs)
correctly; the files are simply missing. See "Contradictions for Manual Review."

---

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

`package.json` confirms: `next@^14.2.0`, `react@^18.3.0`, `typescript@^5.5.0`, `d3@^7.9.0`,
`katex@^0.16.0`, `framer-motion@^11.0.0`, `tailwindcss@^3.4.0`.

`next.config.mjs:3` confirms `output: "export"` (full static site).

`@vercel/analytics@^2.0.1` is present in `package.json` dependencies and is imported in
`src/app/layout.tsx:1`. This was added 2026-05-11 as a portfolio-wide policy. Docs were
partially updated (CLAUDE.md had a strikethrough note) but the Key Decisions table and
AGENTS.md Core Rules still described the pre-analytics state — fixed in this pass.

---

### 4. How to run

**Status:** `drifted` → **fixed**
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

`next.config.mjs:3` sets `output: "export"`. With this setting, `next start` (`npm run start`)
does not work — Next.js static-export mode is incompatible with the production server that
`next start` launches. A user following the README's "Static export" command
(`npm run build && npm run start`) would see an error from Next.js.

**Change made — `README.md` Quick Start / Usage section:**

## Contradictions for manual review

The following files are NOT in the editable set (`README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `DOC-RECONCILIATION.md`, `docs/`), but contain drift a human should fix:

### `IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md`

1. **`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:98`** — File structure diagram lists `data-pipeline/README.md` ("How to regenerate terroir.bin from scratch"), but this file does not exist in the repo. A human should either create `data-pipeline/README.md` or remove the entry from the diagram.

2. **`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:75`** — File structure diagram shows `globe_base.png`. Actual bundled resource is `terroir-ios/Terroir/Resources/globe_base.jpg` (`.jpg`, not `.png`). One-line fix: change `.png` → `.jpg` in the diagram.

3. **`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:475`** — Phase 0 Risks section says: "LZ4 format mismatch: … must explicitly use `lz4.frame.compress()`, not `lz4.block.compress()`." The actual `data-pipeline/05_encode_binary.py:86` uses `lz4.block.compress(data, store_size=False)`, and the Swift side correspondingly uses `COMPRESSION_LZ4_RAW` (block format, not frame). The implementation deliberately uses block on both sides. The roadmap risk note is misleading as written; a human should update it to say block format is used consistently.

4. **`IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md:368`** — Dependencies section specifies `flatbuffers==23.5.26`. The pinned version in `Package.resolved` and `project.yml` is `25.12.19`. The `requirements.txt` uses `flatbuffers>=23.5` (floor-only, not pinned). The roadmap's exact pin is stale; a human should update the version numbers in the pip install example.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats
the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual
current state. It changed no source code, config, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or tests.
Its purpose is to provide an auditable record of what was checked, what drifted, and what was
corrected, so the operator can batch-review with confidence.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status: consistent**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

`src/App.tsx` is the entry point and wires all four views: `DecisionCanvasView`, `SensitivityAnalysisView`,
`TemplateLibraryView`, `DecisionHistoryView`. `src/lib/db.ts`, `src/lib/scoring.ts`, and `src/types/index.ts`
confirm the local-first SQLite multi-criteria decision analysis description. The README intro and CLAUDE.md
overview both match the actual code structure.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status: drifted → fixed**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

`CLAUDE.md` and its embedded portfolio-context block stated "Current Phase: **Phase 0: Foundation**" — the
earliest phase of the implementation roadmap. The code, however, contains fully implemented components
spanning all phases:

- Phase 0 (foundation): `src/lib/db.ts`, `src/lib/scoring.ts`, `src/types/index.ts` ✓
- Phase 1 (decision canvas + scoring matrix): `DecisionCanvasView.tsx`, `ScoringMatrix.tsx`,
  `Sidebar.tsx`, `NewDecisionModal.tsx` ✓
- Phase 2 (sensitivity analysis): `SensitivityAnalysisView.tsx`, `CriteriaWeightSlider.tsx`,
  `RadarChart.tsx`, `RankChangeAlert.tsx`, `src/store/sensitivity-store.ts` ✓
- Phase 3 (templates + history): `TemplateLibraryView.tsx`, `SaveTemplateModal.tsx`,
  `ArchiveDecisionModal.tsx`, `DecisionHistoryView.tsx` ✓
- Beyond roadmap: `src/lib/export.ts`, `src/components/ExportDropdown.tsx` (PDF + CSV export);
  `src/lib/use-keyboard-shortcuts.ts`, `src/components/KeyboardShortcutsModal.tsx` ✓

`package.json` shows `"version": "1.0.0"`, and `git log` includes `615a79c chore: bump version to 1.0.0`.

**Changes made:**
- `CLAUDE.md` line 22: `**Phase 0: Foundation**\nSee IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md...` →
  `**v1.0.0 — Shipped** (all phases complete; see IMPLEMENTATION-ROADMAP.md...)`
- `CLAUDE.md` line 55 (portfolio-context block): same correction applied to the `## Current State` section

---

### 3. Stack

**Status: drifted → fixed**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code (`package.json`)**

`CLAUDE.md` listed stale dependency versions that contradict `package.json`:

| Field | CLAUDE.md claimed | Actual (`package.json`) | Fixed |
|---|---|---|---|
| Frontend | React 18 | react `^19.1.0` | React 19 |
| Charts | Recharts 2.x | recharts `3.8.0` | Recharts 3.x |
| Styling | Tailwind CSS 3.x | tailwindcss `4.2.2` | Tailwind CSS 4.x |
| Build | Vite 5.x | vite `^7.0.4` | Vite 7.x |

`README.md` already had the correct versions (React 19, Tailwind CSS 4, Recharts 3, Vitest 4,
Zustand 5) and required no changes.

**Changes made (two locations in CLAUDE.md):**
- `## Tech Stack` section: four version strings updated as shown above
- `## Stack` section inside `<!-- portfolio-context -->` block: same four strings updated

---

### 4. How to run

**Status: consistent**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code (`package.json` scripts)**

`README.md` and `CLAUDE.md` document three commands:
- `npm run tauri dev` — script `"tauri": "tauri"` + Tauri CLI present ✓
- `npm test` — script `"test": "vitest run"` ✓
- `npm run tauri build` — same `"tauri"` script target ✓

All three commands are defined and match the docs. No changes needed.

---

### 5. Known risks / Do-NOT rules

**Status: consistent**
**Evidence: verified-by-reading-code**

CLAUDE.md's "Do NOT" list prohibits raw SQL in components, localStorage, cloud sync, class components,
and in-DB sensitivity recomputation. Spot-checks confirm the code respects these constraints:
- `src/lib/db.ts` centralizes all SQL; no raw SQL calls found in component files
- `src/store/sensitivity-store.ts` is purely in-memory (no DB writes on weight changes)
- No `localStorage` usage detected in source files

No changes needed.

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `drifted` (partially)
**Evidence:** `src/`, `src-tauri/` contain a full Phase 1–7 feature implementation as claimed by `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md`. The `bf289aa` commit ("Phase 9 — Comprehensive test coverage") was later pruned from the working tree.

There is no `tauri-plugin-sql` dependency anywhere in `Cargo.toml`. All other stack claims are consistent: Tauri 2 (`tauri = { version = "2" }`), Rust 2021 (`edition = "2021"`), React 19 (`react: ^19.1.0`), Tailwind 4 (`tailwindcss: ^4.1.18`), Zustand 5 (`zustand: ^5.0.11`), Ollama REST API (`reqwest` in Cargo.toml + AI component tree).

# DOC-RECONCILIATION

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass. It treats the
source code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so that docs reflect the repo's
actual current state. No code was changed and no builds or tests were run.

---

## Per-claim findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code` — `Conductor/ConductorApp.swift` entry point, `README.md`
intro, and `AGENTS.md` portfolio context all accurately describe a native macOS app that visualizes
Claude Code agentic workflows as interactive force-directed node graphs by reading JSONL logs from
`~/.claude/projects/`.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `drifted` (partially)
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

The README's Features section listed only 6 items, omitting three fully-implemented features
visible in the source tree:

- **Search** — `Conductor/Views/Search/SearchView.swift`, `SearchState.swift`,
  `SearchHistoryView.swift`; uses SwiftData for history persistence.
- **Analytics** — `Conductor/Views/Analytics/AnalyticsView.swift`,
  `AnalyticsChartView.swift`, `ToolPerformanceView.swift`, `AnalyticsCalculator.swift`;
  four tabs (Tokens / Tools / Performance / Trends).
- **Session replay** — `Conductor/State/ReplayController.swift`,
  `Conductor/Views/Replay/ReplayView.swift`, `PlaybackControlsView.swift`.

All three are wired into the SwiftData schema (`ReplayEvent`, `SessionAnalytics`, `SearchHistory`
in `ConductorApp.swift:17-27`) and have dedicated test files (`AnalyticsTests.swift`,
`ReplayControllerTests.swift`, `SearchStateTests.swift`). These are implemented features, not
stubs.

**Changes made:**
- `README.md` Features section: added three bullet points for Search, Analytics, and Replay.
- `AGENTS.md` Current State paragraph: rewrote to enumerate all implemented features rather than
  deferring to a "complete product concept."

---

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

Both `README.md` and `AGENTS.md` Tech Stack tables omitted SwiftData. The app uses SwiftData
extensively: `ModelContainer` initialized in `ConductorApp.swift:15-29`; `@Model` classes for
`Session`, `AgentNode`, `CommandRecord`, `ToolCallRecord`, `SearchHistory`, `SessionAnalytics`,
`ReplayEvent`; `@Query` in analytics views; `ModelContext` in search and app logic.

**Changes made:**
- `README.md` Tech Stack table: added `| Persistence | SwiftData |` row.
- `AGENTS.md` Tech Stack table: same addition.

---

### 4. How to run

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code` — `README.md` correctly documents `xcodegen generate &&
open Conductor.xcodeproj` as the build path. Prerequisites (Xcode 16+, macOS 14.0+, XcodeGen) are
accurate per `project.yml:6` (`xcodeVersion: "16.0"`, `deploymentTarget.macOS: "14.0"`). No
`Package.swift` exists; the Makefile's `swift build/test/run` targets would not work for this
Xcode project, but the Makefile is not a doc file and the README does not reference it.

---

### 5. Known risks / contradictions

**Status:** `drifted`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

The `README.md` Architecture section named three types that do not exist under those names in the
code:

| Claim in README | Reality in code | Evidence |
|---|---|---|
| "`SessionDiscovery` actor that watches the directory for changes" | `enum SessionDiscovery` with static methods — not an `actor`; no directory watching | `Conductor/Parsing/SessionDiscovery.swift:16` |
| "`@MainActor`-isolated `PhysicsEngine`" | Class is named `ForceSimulation` | `Conductor/Graph/ForceSimulation.swift:6` |
| "Node selection publishes to a `SelectionStore`" | No `SelectionStore` exists; selection state is `selectedSessionID`/`selectedNodeID` on `AppState` | `Conductor/State/AppState.swift:6-12` |

Directory monitoring is handled by `LogMonitor` (file-handle polling on a 2-second cycle) wired in
`ConductorApp.startMonitoringIfNeeded()` — not by `SessionDiscovery`.

**Changes made:**
- `README.md` Architecture paragraph: replaced `SessionDiscovery` actor + watches description with
  static scanner + `LogMonitor` polling loop; replaced `PhysicsEngine` with `ForceSimulation`;
  replaced `SelectionStore` with `AppState`.

---

### 6. Next move

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code` — `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` accurately describes
three disposition options (package for distribution, open-source without binary, personal-use tool)

## Contradictions for manual review

### `Makefile` — `swift build` / `swift test` / `swift run` targets

`Makefile:1-12` defines `swift build`, `swift test`, and `swift run` targets. There is no
`Package.swift` in the repo; the project is entirely Xcode-based (`.xcodeproj` generated by
XcodeGen). Running these Make targets will fail. The Makefile is outside the editable doc scope.

**One-line fix a human should make:** replace the Makefile body with `xcodegen generate`,
`xcodebuild -scheme Conductor build`, and `xcodebuild -scheme Conductor test` targets (or remove
the Makefile if it isn't used).

2 desktop app with a Rust backend and a SvelteKit frontend. The tagline "Desktop network discovery
and topology visualizer" matches the entry points and module structure.

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`

README and AGENTS.md claim "Core discovery and port scanning are functional on macOS. IPv6, custom
alert rules, and cross-platform support are not yet implemented."

Code confirms Phases 1–4 are present:
- ARP table scanning: `src-tauri/src/scanner/passive.rs` (macOS path exercised; Linux and Windows
  `#[cfg]` branches exist but are untested/uncertified on those platforms — consistent with the
  "cross-platform support not yet implemented" caveat)
- Ping sweep: `src-tauri/src/scanner/ping.rs`
- Port scanner: `src-tauri/src/scanner/port.rs`
- Alert engine: `src-tauri/src/alerts/engine.rs`, `src-tauri/src/commands/alert.rs`
- OS fingerprinting + device classification: `src-tauri/src/scanner/fingerprint.rs`
- Topology frontend: `src/lib/components/topology/TopologyGraph.svelte`

**Evidence:** `verified-by-reading-code`
