and Svelte 5 (`svelte: "^5.0.0"`). `src-tauri/Cargo.toml` confirms Rust with `rusqlite = "0.32"`
for SQLite. D3 (`d3-force`, `d3-drag`, `d3-selection`, `d3-zoom`) and Tailwind CSS 4 are present
but are implementation details not listed in the README stack table — no change needed.

triggers `beforeDevCommand: "npm run dev"` (Vite) automatically per `src-tauri/tauri.conf.json:8`.

**Evidence:** `src-tauri/src/commands/export.rs` implements `export_devices` (serializes devices +

PCAP format, no `pcap`/`libpcap` crate in `src-tauri/Cargo.toml`, and no packet-capture code
anywhere in the tree. The `csv` crate present in `Cargo.toml` is unused by the export command.

**Evidence:** Same as above — `export.rs` is a JSON serialization round-trip, not a packet capture.

+<!-- portfolio-context:start -->
+# Portfolio Context
+
+## What This Project Is
+
+Echolocate is a Tauri desktop network-discovery and topology visualizer. A Rust backend performs local network scanning, ping/ARP discovery, port checks, and JSON session export while a SvelteKit frontend maps discovered devices and relationships.
+
+## Current State
+
+The repo is a work-in-progress desktop network tool. Core discovery and port scanning are functional on macOS; IPv6, custom alert rules, and cross-platform support are still not implemented. Existing untracked folders are generated artifacts, so this recovery pass should only add the context file.
+
+## Stack
+
+| Layer | Technology |
+|-------|------------|
+| Desktop shell | Tauri 2 |
+| Backend | Rust (network scanning, socket access) |
+| Frontend | SvelteKit (Svelte 5) |
+| Storage | SQLite |
+
+> **Status: Work in Progress** — Core discovery and port scanning are functional on macOS. IPv6, custom alert rules, and cross-platform support are not yet implemented.
+
+## How To Run
+
+```bash
+git clone https://github.com/saagpatel/Echolocate.git
+cd Echolocate
+npm install
+npm run tauri dev
+```
+
+## Known Risks
+
+- Network scanning can be sensitive on real networks; keep scans local and operator-initiated.
+- IPv6, custom alert rules, and cross-platform support are not yet implemented.
+- Scan history is local SQLite state; avoid destructive resets unless explicitly requested.
+- Generated `artifacts` and `test-results` folders are local outputs and should not be swept into source commits.
+
+## Next Recommended Move
+
+Add only the context file for this recovery pass, then continue with macOS discovery stability before expanding IPv6, alert rules, or cross-platform support.
+
+<!-- portfolio-context:end -->

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the
code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current
state. It changed no source code and ran no builds or tests. The purpose is to serve as an auditable
record of what was checked, what drifted, and what was fixed.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:** `src/main.ts` (entry point), `rust/src/lib.rs` (WASM exports), `src/generation/WasmBridge.ts`
(Rust/WASM bridge), `src/engine/` (Three.js scene/chunk/water), `src/generation/` (noise + erosion
pipeline). The README description — "browser-based procedural terrain generator, Rust/WASM pipeline,
Three.js rendering" — matches the actual code structure exactly.

Two sub-claims are unverifiable from code alone:
- "5–20× faster than JavaScript" — no benchmark exists in the repo; not refuted either.
  (`unverifiable-because-no-benchmark-code`)
- "60fps" — stated as a target, not measured in code. (`unverifiable-because-runtime-metric`)

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `drifted` (in AGENTS.md) + `drifted` (in docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md)
**Evidence:**
- All features listed in the README are implemented in code (verified: noise types in
  `rust/src/lib.rs:70-76`, 12 biomes in `rust/src/biome/classifier.rs:6-19`, erosion in
  `rust/src/erosion/hydraulic.rs`, 8 presets in `src/ui/PresetGallery.ts:9-108`, export tools in
  `src/utils/export.ts`).
- `docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md` explicitly declares status "Wind-down" with no planned Phase 2.
- `AGENTS.md` "Current State" omitted the wind-down status; "Next Recommended Move" said "resume
  the next active task" — contradicting the archived disposition.
- `docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md` "Last known-good reference" table cited `1a2f559` as the last master
  commit but HEAD is `d585660` (three doc/chore commits landed after the posture was written).

- `AGENTS.md`: Added wind-down note to "Current State" section.
  Before: *no mention of archived status*
  After: *added "This project is in wind-down. See `docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md`..."*

  Before: *"Use this context... to resume the next active task, then promote..."*
  After: *"This project is archived — no active development is planned. Refer to `docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md`..."*

  Before: `1a2f559` chore(repo): prune nonessential files

### 3. Stack

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence:**
- Three.js r170+: `package.json:17` `"three": "^0.170.0"` ✓
- Rust → WASM (wasm-pack): `rust/Cargo.toml:7-8` `crate-type = ["cdylib"]` + `wasm-bindgen` dep ✓

### 4. How to run

- `npm run build:wasm` → `"build:wasm": "cd rust && ./build.sh"` ✓
- `npm install` → standard package manager install ✓

Note (not drifted, informational): The project uses pnpm as its primary package manager
(`package.json` has a `pnpm` config block; `docs/ARCHIVE-POSTURE.md` uses `pnpm` commands;
`src/generation/WasmBridge.ts:55` error message says `pnpm build:wasm`). The README lists pnpm as a
prerequisite but shows `npm run` commands in examples. This is not factually wrong (npm commands
work) but `pnpm` equivalents would be more consistent.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current state. It changed no source code, config, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or tests. Its purpose is to provide an auditable record of what was found and what was changed.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is
**Status:** `consistent` (with corrections — see below)  
**Evidence:** `Wavelength/App/WavelengthApp.swift`, `Wavelength/Core/SignalRegistry.swift`, `Wavelength/Metal/SpectrogramRenderer.swift`  
The app description ("real-time electromagnetic spectrum visualizer for iOS") is accurate. However, the README Architecture section named the sensor actors and central registry incorrectly (see Claim 3 — Stack).

### 2. Current state
**Status:** `drifted` → **fixed**  
**Evidence:** `Wavelength/` directory contains 35 Swift source files + 17 test files. `Wavelength/UI/SettingsView.swift`, `Wavelength/UI/OnboardingView.swift`, `Wavelength/Contextual/ContextualEngine.swift`, `Wavelength/Metal/SpectrogramRenderer.swift`, `Wavelength/Metal/SpectrogramTexture.swift` all fully implemented. `WavelengthTests/` contains 17 test files.  
Both `CLAUDE.md` and its embedded Portfolio Context said "Phase 0: Foundation (Weeks 1–2)" — but Phases 0, 1, 2, and 3 are all implemented. App Store metadata (`APPSTORE-METADATA.md`), privacy manifest (`Wavelength/Resources/PrivacyInfo.xcprivacy`), and submission checklist are present. TestFlight and App Store submission are the only remaining items.

**Changes:**
- `CLAUDE.md` "Current Phase" section: `Phase 0: Foundation (Weeks 1–2)` → `Phases 0–3 complete. … Remaining: TestFlight beta testing and App Store submission.`
- `CLAUDE.md` Portfolio Context "Current State": same update

### 3. Stack
**Status:** `drifted` → **fixed** (three sub-claims)

#### 3a. GRDB.swift version
**Evidence:** `Wavelength.xcodeproj/project.xcworkspace/xcshareddata/swiftpm/Package.resolved:8` — `"version": "7.10.0"`  
Both `CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack and Portfolio Context Stack listed `GRDB.swift: ~6.x`.  
**Changes:**
- `CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack: `GRDB.swift: ~6.x` → `GRDB.swift: ~7.x`
- `CLAUDE.md` Portfolio Context Stack: same update

#### 3b. Satellite package name
**Evidence:** `Package.resolved:22-30` — identity `"satellitekit"`, location `https://github.com/gavineadie/SatelliteKit`, version `"2.1.1"`. The planned `SwiftyTLE` package is not present.  
Both `CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack and Portfolio Context Stack listed `SwiftyTLE: latest`.  
**Changes:**
- `CLAUDE.md` Tech Stack: `SwiftyTLE: latest — TLE parsing + SGP4 propagator` → `SatelliteKit: ~2.x (gavineadie/SatelliteKit) — TLE parsing + SGP4 propagator`
- `CLAUDE.md` Portfolio Context Stack: same update

#### 3c. Texture pixel format
**Evidence:** `Wavelength/Metal/SpectrogramTexture.swift:24` — `pixelFormat: .rgba8Unorm`; log statement at line 52 confirms `"RGBA8Unorm"`.  
`README.md` Features section and Architecture section both said `RGBA16F`.  
**Changes:**
- `README.md` Features bullet: `RGBA16F` → `RGBA8Unorm`

#### 3d. Alamofire version
**Status:** `consistent`  
**Evidence:** `Package.resolved` shows Alamofire 5.11.1, within the `~5.9` compatible range documented.

### 4. How to run
**Status:** `consistent`  
**Evidence:** `Wavelength.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj` exists; README quick-start instructions (`open Wavelength.xcodeproj`, deploy to physical device) match the project structure and app requirements.

### 5. Known risks / Do NOT constraints
**Status:** `consistent`  
**Evidence:** The "Do NOT" section in `CLAUDE.md` (no CocoaPods/Carthage, no UserDefaults for signal data, SPM only, no raw BT identifiers, cache TTLs, no mmWave in v1, no gamification) all remain valid design constraints. The code confirms SPM-only (`Package.resolved`), GRDB for storage, and privacy-mode BT handling (`Wavelength/Sensing/BluetoothScanner.swift`).

### 6. Next move
**Status:** `drifted` → **fixed** (subsumed by Current State fix above)  
The Portfolio Context "Next Recommended Move" was intentionally vague ("resume the next active task") — left unchanged as `unverifiable` (forward-looking). The `CLAUDE.md` Current Phase section now accurately names what remains: TestFlight beta and App Store submission.

The README Architecture paragraph named the sensor components using planned names that differ from what was implemented.

**Evidence:** `Wavelength/Sensing/BluetoothScanner.swift` (not `BluetoothAdapter`), `WiFiScanner.swift` (not `WiFiAdapter`), `CellularMonitor.swift` (not `CellularAdapter`), `LocationMonitor.swift` (not `LocationAdapter`), `Core/SignalRegistry.swift` (not `SignalAggregator`).

**Changes:**
- `README.md` Architecture paragraph: `BluetoothAdapter` → `BluetoothScanner`, `WiFiAdapter` → `WiFiScanner`, `CellularAdapter` → `CellularMonitor`, `LocationAdapter` → `LocationMonitor`, `SignalAggregator` → `SignalRegistry`, "Four sensor adapters" → "Four sensor actors"

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by a `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass. That pass treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current state. It changed no source code, configuration, tests, or lockfiles, and ran no builds or tests. Its purpose is to give any reviewer a timestamped, evidence-cited audit trail of what docs matched the code and what was corrected.

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`

**Basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

The README describes KnowledgeCore as "a local-first, encrypted knowledge vault for ingesting, indexing, and querying documents." All core capabilities are present in the codebase:

- Vault init/open: `crates/kc_core/src/vault.rs`
- Ingest pipeline: `crates/kc_core/src/ingest.rs`, `crates/kc_extract/src/`
- FTS5 index: `crates/kc_index/src/fts.rs`
- LanceDB vector index: `crates/kc_index/src/vector.rs`
- Ask mode (retrieved-only, citation-enforced): `crates/kc_ask/src/ask.rs`
- Export + verifier: `crates/kc_core/src/export.rs`, `crates/kc_cli/src/verifier.rs`
- Desktop UI (Tauri 2): `apps/desktop/src-tauri/src/commands.rs`

No change made.

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent`

**Basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

The GA decision record (`knowledgecore-docpack/docs/14-ga-decision-record.md`) records NO-GO for public GA and GO for internal pilot at v0.1.0, with blocking conditions around code-signing and notarization. The README does not make GA release claims — it describes features, all of which exist in code.

No change made.

### 5. Known risks (code↔doc contradictions)

**Status:** `drifted` — **fixed**

**Basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

**Before:**
> `README.md:16` — `- **Recovery escrow** — pluggable escrow backends: AWS KMS, Azure, GCP, HSM, or local`

**After:**
> `README.md:16` — `- **Recovery escrow** — AWS KMS backend (real SDK); Azure, GCP, and HSM adapters use local filesystem emulation only (no cloud SDK)`

**Evidence:**
- `crates/kc_core/Cargo.toml:9-11` — AWS SDKs (`aws-sdk-kms`, `aws-sdk-s3`, `aws-sdk-secretsmanager`) are real dependencies.
- `crates/kc_core/src/recovery_escrow_azure.rs:27-31,77-88` — Azure provider: `available = configured && emulated`; `write()` returns `KC_RECOVERY_ESCROW_UNAVAILABLE` error when `KC_RECOVERY_ESCROW_AZURE_EMULATE_DIR` is not set. No Azure SDK dependency in `Cargo.toml`.
- `crates/kc_core/src/recovery_escrow_gcp.rs:29-34` — GCP provider: same emulation-only pattern; `KC_RECOVERY_ESCROW_GCP_EMULATE_DIR` env var required. No GCP SDK dependency in `Cargo.toml`.
- `crates/kc_core/src/recovery_escrow_hsm.rs:27-32,50` — HSM provider: same emulation-only pattern; `KC_RECOVERY_ESCROW_HSM_EMULATE_DIR` env var required.

Azure, GCP, and HSM backends are **filesystem emulation adapters** that error at runtime when the emulation env var is absent. They are not connected to real cloud provider SDKs.

---

### 6. Next move

**Status:** `consistent`

**Basis:** `verified-by-reading-code`

The README does not include a roadmap or "next steps" section. The blocking items for GA (code-signing, notarization) are captured in `knowledgecore-docpack/docs/14-ga-decision-record.md` — a docpack file outside the editability scope of this pass, and appropriate for internal tracking rather than the public README.

No change made.

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the
code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current
state. No code was changed and no builds or tests were run — all evidence was gathered by reading
source files, manifests, and git history.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is
**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `README.md` intro, `CLAUDE.md` Overview, and `AGENTS.md` Default Mode all accurately
describe mcpforge as a Python CLI that generates runnable FastMCP 3.x MCP servers from plain-English
descriptions. `src/mcpforge/cli.py:653` confirms the `generate` command entry point.
`pyproject.toml:4` confirms `description = "Generate complete, runnable FastMCP 3.x MCP servers..."`.

### 2. Current state
**Status: drifted → fixed**
Evidence: `pyproject.toml:3` sets `version = "0.3.0"`. `src/mcpforge/__init__.py:13` sets
`__version__ = "0.3.0"`. `docs/CURRENT-STATE.md` (last updated 2026-05-10) documents PyPI publish
success for `fastmcp-builder==0.3.0`.

**Drifted:** `CLAUDE.md` described the current phase as "Post-foundation stabilization / release
readiness" and explicitly referenced deciding "whether the current `0.2.0` state should be
published/tagged" — stale by one full release cycle. Similarly, `CLAUDE.md`'s Portfolio Context
"Next Recommended Move" still said "The next decision is whether to publish/tag the current `0.2.0`
state."

**Fixed in `CLAUDE.md`:**
- Current Phase: `"Post-foundation stabilization / release readiness"` → `"Active — v0.3.0 published to PyPI (fastmcp-builder)"`; body text updated to reflect v0.3.0 and provider matrix expansion focus.
- Portfolio Context "Current State": label updated to `"Active — v0.3.0 published to PyPI as fastmcp-builder"`.
- Portfolio Context "Next Recommended Move": v0.2.0 decision language replaced with current frontier (OpenAI smoke gate).

**Also drifted:** `docs/ROADMAP-v0.3.md:45` said "Before tagging `v0.3.0`, run:" — but `v0.3.0` is
already tagged and published per `git log` (`72d2c01 chore(release): prepare fastmcp-builder v0.3.0`).

**Fixed in `docs/ROADMAP-v0.3.md`:**
- Release Gate header: `"Before tagging v0.3.0, run:"` → `"Release gate for v0.3.0 (completed 2026-05-10). Commands run before tagging:"`

### 3. Stack
**Status: drifted → fixed**
Evidence: `pyproject.toml:25` specifies `fastmcp>=3.2.3`. Three locations in `CLAUDE.md` and one
location in `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` claimed `FastMCP 3.1.x`.

**Fixed in `CLAUDE.md`:**
- Tech Stack line 8: `"FastMCP: 3.1.x (standalone, PrefectHQ/fastmcp)"` → `"FastMCP: 3.2.x ..."`
- Key Decisions table: `"FastMCP 3.1.x standalone"` → `"FastMCP 3.2.x standalone"`
- Portfolio Context Stack: `"FastMCP: 3.1.x (standalone, PrefectHQ/fastmcp)"` → `"FastMCP: 3.2.x ..."`

**Also drifted:** `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` "Last known reference" table said
`"Python 3.11+ (uv-managed)"` but `pyproject.toml:7` requires `requires-python = ">=3.12"`.

**Fixed in `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md`:**
- `"Python 3.11+ (uv-managed)"` → `"Python 3.12+ (uv-managed)"`

**Also drifted:** `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md` "Current state in one paragraph" listed
`` `mcpforge describe` `` as a CLI tool, but no such command exists. `src/mcpforge/cli.py` defines:
`generate`, `update`, `validate`, `version`, `list`, `inspect`, `doctor`, `init`. The correct
command for describing a generated server shape is `mcpforge inspect`.

**Fixed in `docs/PORTFOLIO-DISPOSITION.md`:**
- `` `mcpforge describe` `` → `` `mcpforge inspect` ``

**Note:** `README.md` Tech Stack table lists "FastMCP 3.x" (not a specific minor version) —
consistent with the actual `>=3.2.3` constraint. `pyproject.toml` also includes `openai>=2.36.0`
and `pyyaml>=6.0.3` as runtime deps not shown in the README table; the OpenAI provider is
mentioned in the Generation row as gated, and `pyyaml` is an internal parsing dep not
user-visible — leaving README table as-is.

### 4. How to run
**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `pyproject.toml:33-34` defines console scripts `mcpforge = "mcpforge.cli:cli"` and
`mcpforge-server = "mcpforge.mcp_server:mcp.run"`. `README.md` install command
`uv tool install fastmcp-builder` matches `pyproject.toml:2` `name = "fastmcp-builder"`.
All flags documented in `README.md` (--dry-run, --no-execute, --strict, --from-openapi,
--language, --auth-profile, --middleware-profile, --provider) confirmed present in
`src/mcpforge/cli.py:509-652`. `AGENTS.md` verification baseline commands (`uv run pytest`,
`uv run ruff check .`) are consistent with `pyproject.toml` dev dependencies.

### 5. Known risks
**Status: consistent**
Evidence: `CLAUDE.md` "Do NOT" guardrails and `docs/CURRENT-STATE.md` "Known Risks" section are
accurate. OpenAI provider gating is reflected correctly in `README.md` (generation row mentions
gated smokes) and in `src/mcpforge/cli.py:530` (`help="Generation provider. OpenAI is gated until structured-output smokes land."`).

### 6. Next move
**Status: drifted → fixed** (see claim 2 above for details)
The demonstrably incomplete work — per `docs/CURRENT-STATE.md:Recommended Next Moves` and
`docs/ROADMAP-v0.3.md:Remaining v0.3 Work` — is: add `OPENAI_API_KEY`, replenish Anthropic credits,
run hosted smoke matrix, then ungate OpenAI. Fixed in `CLAUDE.md` Next Recommended Move (see above).

+## What's in here
+
+- **Watchlist** — ticker table with live price data, TanStack Query polling every 30 s
+- **Scanner** — daily and weekly scans surface tickers matching configurable criteria; results filterable by scan type
+- **Alerts** — triggered on >5% day moves and >3× volume spikes; dismissible inline or via the Alerts tab
+- **News** — RSS-fed ticker-scoped news panel
+- **Freshness indicator** — shows data staleness in the header
+- **Dark/light theme toggle**
+- **Background worker** (`worker/index.ts`) — cron-scheduled refresh every 15 min during market hours, daily S&P scan at 6:30 AM PT, weekly full scan Sunday 8 PM PT
+
+Persistence: SQLite via Drizzle ORM + better-sqlite3. Data file lives in `data/`.

+- Recharts, Zustand

# DOC-RECONCILIATION.md

This file was generated by the `/doc-truth-up` documentation-reconciliation pass, which treats the code as read-only ground truth and edits only documentation so it reflects the repo's actual current state. It changed no code and ran no builds or tests. It exists so reviewers can audit exactly what was checked, what was changed, and what requires human follow-up.

---

## Per-Claim Findings

### 1. What it is

**Status:** `consistent`
**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code

README and CLAUDE.md both describe thought-trails as a local Tauri 2 desktop app that streams Ollama chain-of-thought tokens, parses them into typed nodes (claim/evidence/backtrack/conclusion), and renders a live D3 force-directed graph. This matches:
- `src-tauri/src/lib.rs` — registers `start_reasoning_stream`, `cancel_stream`, `list_ollama_models`, `check_ollama_health`, `save_session`, `load_session`, `delete_session`, `list_sessions`
- `src/App.tsx` — mounts `GraphCanvas`, `PromptPanel`, `SessionSidebar`, `ComparisonView`, etc.
- `src-tauri/src/cot_parser.rs` — heuristic Rust parser emitting `ReasoningEvent` structs

No changes made.

---

### 2. Current state

**Status:** `consistent` (README) / `drifted` (CLAUDE.md)
**Evidence basis:** verified-by-reading-code

README accurately claims the project is feature-complete across Phases 0–4 plus hardening. All features are verified in source:
- Replay: `src/hooks/use-replay.ts`, `src/components/replay-controls.tsx`
- Session persistence: `src-tauri/src/session.rs`, `src/hooks/use-sessions.ts`
- Graph search: `src/hooks/use-graph-search.ts`, `src/components/graph-search.tsx`
- Node detail panel + ancestry: `src/components/node-detail-panel.tsx`
- Collapsible subtrees: `filterCollapsed` in `src/lib/graph-builder.ts`; `collapseAll`/`expandAll` in `src/App.tsx`
- Tree layout: `src/hooks/use-tree-layout.ts`
- Multi-model comparison: `src/components/comparison-view.tsx`, `comparison-prompt.tsx`, `comparison-stats.tsx`

CLAUDE.md `## Known Issues` contained a false claim: *"Replay mode timing is fixed-interval; no variable-speed playback."* The code implements four replay speeds (0.5×, 1×, 2×, 4×) via `type ReplaySpeed = 0.5 | 1 | 2 | 4` and a `cycleSpeed` function in `src/hooks/use-replay.ts:6–7`. This was also present in the `## Known Risks` block inside the `<!-- portfolio-context -->` section.

**Changed:**
- `CLAUDE.md` `## Known Issues`: removed stale bullet "Replay mode timing is fixed-interval; no variable-speed playback"
- `CLAUDE.md` `## Known Risks` (portfolio-context block): removed the same stale bullet

---
